* [v4] feat(theme): Content width css variable for easier customization (#3767)
* feat(theme): Content width css variable for easier customization
This moves the content width that was used throughout nextra
`max-w-[90rem]` to a css variable. This way the changing the value in
the future should be easier, but it also makes it possible to customize
the max width of the content for people using nextra without needing to
overload a tailwind class in a hacky way.

* [v4] feat(theme): Content width css variable for easier customization (#3767)
* feat(theme): Content width css variable for easier customization
This moves the content width that was used throughout nextra
`max-w-[90rem]` to a css variable. This way the changing the value in
the future should be easier, but it also makes it possible to customize
the max width of the content for people using nextra without needing to
overload a tailwind class in a hacky way.

* Add ISSUE_TEMPLATE and PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE
Add ISSUE_TEMPLATE and PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE to the .github directory. These templates are designed to assist contributors in reporting issues and submitting pull requests by providing guidance on the necessary information to include. This helps streamline the contribution process for both issue reporting and pull requests.

* [v4] feat(theme): Content width css variable for easier customization (#3767)
* feat(theme): Content width css variable for easier customization
This moves the content width that was used throughout nextra
`max-w-[90rem]` to a css variable. This way the changing the value in
the future should be easier, but it also makes it possible to customize
the max width of the content for people using nextra without needing to
overload a tailwind class in a hacky way.

* [v4] feat(theme): Content width css variable for easier customization (#3767)
* feat(theme): Content width css variable for easier customization
This moves the content width that was used throughout nextra
`max-w-[90rem]` to a css variable. This way the changing the value in
the future should be easier, but it also makes it possible to customize
the max width of the content for people using nextra without needing to
overload a tailwind class in a hacky way.

* [v4] feat(theme): Content width css variable for easier customization (#3767)
* feat(theme): Content width css variable for easier customization
This moves the content width that was used throughout nextra
`max-w-[90rem]` to a css variable. This way the changing the value in
the future should be easier, but it also makes it possible to customize
the max width of the content for people using nextra without needing to
overload a tailwind class in a hacky way.

* [v4] feat(theme): Content width css variable for easier customization (#3767)
* feat(theme): Content width css variable for easier customization
This moves the content width that was used throughout nextra
`max-w-[90rem]` to a css variable. This way the changing the value in
the future should be easier, but it also makes it possible to customize
the max width of the content for people using nextra without needing to
overload a tailwind class in a hacky way.

Nextra
======

[](https://github.com/shuding/nextra?screenshot=true#nextra)

Simple, powerful and flexible site generation framework with everything you love from Next.js.

Documentation
-------------

[](https://github.com/shuding/nextra?screenshot=true#documentation)

[https://nextra.site](https://nextra.site/)

Development
-----------

[](https://github.com/shuding/nextra?screenshot=true#development)

### Installation

[](https://github.com/shuding/nextra?screenshot=true#installation)

The Nextra repository uses [PNPM Workspaces](https://pnpm.io/workspaces) and [Turborepo](https://github.com/vercel/turborepo). To install dependencies, run `pnpm install` in the project root directory.

### Build Nextra Core

[](https://github.com/shuding/nextra?screenshot=true#build-nextra-core)

```shell
pnpm --filter nextra build
```

Watch mode: `pnpm --filter nextra dev`

### Build Nextra Theme

[](https://github.com/shuding/nextra?screenshot=true#build-nextra-theme)

```shell
pnpm --filter nextra-theme-docs build
```

### Development

[](https://github.com/shuding/nextra?screenshot=true#development-1)

You can also debug them together with a website locally. For instance, to start `examples/docs` locally, run

```shell
pnpm --filter example-docs dev
```

Any change to `example/docs` will be re-rendered instantly.

If you update the core or theme packages, a rebuild is required. Or you can use the watch mode for both nextra and the theme in separated terminals.
